Well, I certainly didn&#x27;t want to. I do wish this model came with two handles, but instead my wife and I just take turns and switch out our own heads. Awesome brush, but honestly i don&#x27;t use the &#x27;sensitive&#x27;, &#x27;massage&#x27; or &#x27;Max Care&#x27; options so I guess I&#x27;ll be looking for the less expensive one next time.</li>
    <li> This toothbrush cleans well, but only lasted me 2 years, I do also replace the brush heads every 3 months or so, and I traveled with it once for two weeks.&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;m disappointed that this $120 toothbrush only lasted 2 years + the brush heads I replaced, definitely too costly. Now I know how electric toothbrush can stop working in 2 years, I will not buy another expensive toothbrush.</li>
    <li> My electric toothbrush holder died after 2 years.  For the money I expect a product to last longer.  I did like it while it worked and my dentist could tell my teeth were in better condition (I brush too hard with regular tooth brushes).  I would not buy again though due to the price.</li>
    <li> Replacement love this product.</li>
    <li> I upgraded to this model after my old elite bit the dust, and I couldn&#x27;t be happier. I feel like I&#x27;ve just left the dentist after each use.  The customer service crew couldn&#x27;t be friendlier or more helpful - very pleased with this purchase.</li>
    <li> I&#x27;ve used Sonicare rechargeable toothbrushes since they were introduced.  No problems with ANY of them.  This system with the Sanitizer is the best one yet.   No Bulky holder for the toothbrush that gets filled with...and has to be   cleaned weekly, and the compact brush heads are great for smaller mouths  and control when brushing.  Flex care is the best.  All my Sonicare Batteries have held up. I think it may be user specific for those  that complain about the battery The battery has always served me well when I use it on the road.  The noise? All electronic toothbrushes I&#x27;ve tried are noisy.  Without my Sonicare, I&#x27;d be cleaning my teeth in a glass.   I&#x27;ll trade noise, which I hate, for in tact teeth anytime!</li>
    <li> So, I have been using electric toothbrushes for a few years. I have tried various brands; you know, the ones when you purchase another toothbrush when the battery dies because its too much of a hassle to get to the battery. Needless to say, there wasn&#x27;t an inexpensive brand I have not tried.     My routine visits to the dentist have been less than desirable. I have had cavities and a root canal. What prompted me in considering the FlexCare stemmed from a close, self-examination of my teeth and gums and I was displeased.     I booked an appointment to the dentist but it was a TWO MONTH wait time and I needed to do something ASAP. So, after research, the reviews really spoked for themselves. I searched Amazon and used Google to get the low down on the best at home cleaning options and mostly all pointed to Sonicare products.     I particurlarly chose this brand do the sanitizing feature. Call me a sucker for gimmicks but I am a huge germ-a-phobe. Plus being able to have two brush heads in the sanitizing unit allowed for me to use different brushes during the morning and evening...another plus!     The unit itself allows for multiple cleaning options: (basic clean, sensitive setting, message setting, 1 minute clean and 3 minute clean).     The performance of this toothbrush is unmatched. The power actually caught me off-guard. Of course, I made the terrible mistake of taking the toothbrush out of my mouth during operation...HUGE MESS. The first two brushes were noticeable but by the third day, I handled all settings with no problems.     In two weeks of usage I could see a difference in my teeth. A natural whiteness appeared, my teeth FELT clean, and my gums and tongue have actually benefit from usage. My hope is that with continued usage by the time my dental appointment arrives, I will not need root scaling/planing and that my plague build-up will be minimal.     Obviously proper oral health and regular dental visits are the best method. However, for those of us thatfeel off track, you first two steps is to get this toothbrush (and don&#x27;t look back) and find a dentist you feel comfortable with and create a plan to regain optimal oral health.     I have no \\&quot;cons\\&quot; on this product. I know many were not happy with the non-replaceable battery. I purchased this unit that gave TWO Flexcare toothbrushes along with two cleaning heads. If I can get 5 year usage, I will be pleased.     I would recommend users couple the FlexCare along with the Waterpick Ultra Jet (another excellent product). Tom&#x27;s of Maine makes excellent mouthwashes that do not include alcohol or saccharin. Colgate Total appears to get the highest reviews for cleaning and post-cleaning protection. I also use Sensodyne&#x27;s Pronamel toothpaste.     I cannot reiterate enough that with the power the FlexCare provides, I cannot imagine any other brush really doing an effective job at cleaning. I will definitely come back and following up after my second dental dentist to discuss improvements with using the FlexCare.     If you are hesitant in buying, just think dropping this amount of money on a toothbrush will likely push you to to upkeep a regular brushing habit. LOL     Gave it 5 stars because the performance is unmatched. Considering the higher price, most cannot afford to have this even though it should be attainable and because of that, overall I would rate 4.5 stars.</li>
    <li> If you&#x27;ve never owned a Sonicare, you will probably find this toothbrush to be really noisy and much heavier than a normal toothbrush, but that&#x27;s because it actually cleans significantly better than a toothbrush, leaving you with that \\&quot;just got a dental cleaning\\&quot; feeling -- versus those other vibrating/rotating brushes that are basically designed for the lazy brusher and don&#x27;t really clean any better. (If you&#x27;ve owned an earlier model, you&#x27;ll find this one is lighter and quieter than those. It&#x27;s worth the upgrade!)    It&#x27;s not loud enough to wake up my wife while I get ready in the morning -- whereas my electric shaver is louder and will wake her up.    As for battery life, I&#x27;ve been using this model for 9 months with no problems. It can easily go a week between charging (even now), and I&#x27;ve never needed the travel charger that it comes with (but it&#x27;s nice to have one should I be going somewhere for more than a week). I&#x27;ve read the manual, and it is true that the battery cannot be replaced once dead, but I&#x27;m confident I&#x27;ll be able to get at least another year before that happens. The battery seems as good today as it was when I first opened it -- wish I could say the same for my laptop and cordless tools.</li>
    <li> I have been thinking about getting an electric toothbrush for years.  I decided that for my birthday I would treat myself to this one.      The first decision I had to make was a rotating head (Oral B) or back-and-forth (Sonicare). I went by word of mouth and reading reviews.  Surprisingly, everyone I know has a sonicare toothbrush.  The second decision was whether or not to get the bells and whistles or a basic brush.  I liked all the different settings this one offered.  I have sensitive teeth and was worried about agitating my teeth.  It helped that it was on sale for the same price as the one without the sanitizer.  I have actually been able to switch to regular toothpaste instead of sensitive toothpaste.    My only concern was of the reviews that mentioned the toothbrush being loud.  As a newbie, I&#x27;ve found it to be quite manageable.  I can brush my teeth in the morning and not worry about my boyfriend waking up.  The most difficult thing to figure out was how to keep all the toothpaste in my mouth will transitioning the brush around my mouth.  The brush head is small enough to keep your mouth closed and still maneuver around.    Overall, I&#x27;m kicking myself for not making the purchase earlier.  I&#x27;m getting addicted to the dentist clean feel.  I now brush 4 times a day instead of 2.</li>
    <li> Frankly, I can&#x27;t say enough about this toothbrush...  First, though, my teeth have been a mess for years.  This is mostly my fault due to a fear of dentist for a variety of reasons (including the time when the dentist inadvertently stuck me in the arm with a novocaine needle) which kept me from the dentist&#x27;s office for a long time.  My wife finally convinced me to go to a dentist, and I found a terrific one.  Anyway, after a lot of work, my teeth are finally nice and healthy, and I bought this toothbrush - Philips Sonicare FlexCare Rechargeable Sonic Toothbrush with Sanitizer - to help keep my teeth in top shape.  I couldn&#x27;t be happier!  After every use, I feel like I&#x27;ve just had my teeth professionally cleaned, and it&#x27;s actually a lot of fun using the thing.  I usually start off with the regular \\&quot;Clean\\&quot; function taking care to brush each \\&quot;quad\\&quot; section in my mouth (I usually do this twice), followed by the \\&quot;Message\\&quot; section to go over my gums.  The end result is a squeakly clean, refreshed mouth that feels great.  If you get this toothbrush, you may experience some tingling around your gums when you first start out, but you&#x27;ll quickly get used to it.  Oh, and I also like the onboard sanitizer to keep the brush clean and germ free.  This is truly a wonderful product if you want to keep  your teeth strong and healthy, and to give you a smile that&#x27;ll light up a room!</li>
    <li> I have enjoyed using electric toothbrushes for years as I feel they are far superior to manual ones. At the recommendation of my dentist recently, I decided to give the Sonicare a try. The design is different and the brush is a different shape, more like a traditional toothbrush. The rapid vibration takes a bit to get use to but there is no denying the exceptionally clean feeling after the 2 minute timer cuts the power cycle. It is the closest clean to the \\&quot;6 month\\&quot; Dental cleaning I have experienced. I recomment this product for it&#x27;s ability, design and features although I am unsure what difference the \\&quot;UV light\\&quot; sanitizer really makes. There are plenty of features to utilize like the \\&quot;quadrant timer\\&quot; which alows you to break down the 2 minute timer into 4 sections for the most effective and even brushing. The brush IS very pricey but consider this product if you really care about your dental upkeep.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;****Amendment****  2 1/2 years later and this toothbrush system is still working flawlessly. Awesome investment!  : )</li>
    <li> This Philips Sonicare FlexCare is an update to my previous sonicare.    The massage cycle is a treat to my gums. I like the fact there are options to cleaning and massage cycles.  The sanitizer is a plus.  I have been very pleased with this product.</li>
    <li> I had the Intelliclen system I was happy with it in till I learned that sonicare no longer made brush heads for it what ever reason which was stupid but whatever I think it was mainly because they wanted people to upgrade.... It dose come with two brush size&#x27;s I personally only the bigger one it also come&#x27;s  with a smaller one.     <li> I&#x27;ve used several Sonicare toothbrushes in the past and feel like they are the reason I&#x27;ve such healthy gums.  As a physician I&#x27;m very aware that healthy gums are one of the most important things for HEART health, too!  So I really have valued my Sonicare brushes.  And at the age of 58 I have perfect gums and perfect heart health, inspite of being overweight and sedentary.    However, I&#x27;m very disappointed in this new model.  First off the brush head is really small.  I cannot believe the difference in the amount of gunk that remains between my teeth after using the unit the full cleaning program.  I&#x27;ve actually gone through several cycles and the trash remains.  If I look in my makeup mirror I can actually see it!  Now don&#x27;t you think two full cycles with a Sonicare should get that out???  I guarantee my old one would have.      So, I have to floss more diligently than I have in years now.  It seems to me that this unit cleans tooth surfaces just fine, but that is not what I use an electric toothbrush for.  I want the gum stimulation, which is adequate by virtue of the sonic vibration--you don&#x27;t need that silly \\&quot;massage\\&quot; setting.  And I want really excellent crud removal from between teeth, which I find inadequate with this unit.    As to the brush sanitizer:  I figure if that nasty sludge that used to build up in the handle of my old Sonicare didn&#x27;t kill me, surely I don&#x27;t need an infrared cleaner for the brush head!  Perhaps if I had gum disease, or some disease spread by oral contamination, I&#x27;d think it was a good idea, but frankly?  I think it&#x27;s unnecessary.</li>
    <li> This is my first electric toothbrush, been using it for a year now and I love it. My dentist recommended the switch to this electric because I couldn&#x27;t break the bad habit of brushing too hard at the gumline. This brush gets my teeth \\&quot;dentist clean\\&quot; while being gentler on my gums, with much less sensitivity overall as an added bonus.  For those used to small toothbrushes (size 30), the compact head works nicely. The full size is much too large for me, but works perfectly for my husband. We store both heads in the sanitizer and run it after each round of brushing; tried running it once a day as stated in the manual but noticed some bacterial growth at the base of the brushes (where the color code rings snap on) after a few days, so went back to twice daily and all was well.  The travel charger, case and head covers are handy - no more of those awkward, giant &#x27;snap in&#x27; travel toothbrushes!  The unit is pricey, and having to change out the heads every three months means another $30 or so per person a year, but for us the benefits have been worth the extra cost.</li>

    <li> I&#x27;ve owned several of these over the years. An innovative and terrific design and product. Consumer Reports gave it and the Rotary  thumbs up. I bought the rotary Braum for a test. Forget it. CR missed this one by a mile.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt; The one I have now is a HX6932 with the sealed top to keep the crud out. It broke outside of warranty so I bought a new one. For a tool that&#x27;s used 2-3 times a day I&#x27;m a happy camper. My shop tools should be this good.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt; So I cut it open for a post mortem exam. A tiny screw came loose that clamps the vibrating steel brush rod to the guts. This is a fix for broken units where the steel brush post wobbles around only! Drill a 3/16\\&quot; hole in the case 1.5\\&quot; below the end of the steel brush rod. The on/off switch is facing you. Get a tube of Locktite blue from your local auto parts supply store and put a drop on the loose Phillips screw before re- installing. Then plug the hole with Goop marine glue from Lowes. Good as new.er I hope.No warranty here especially if your clumsy.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Everybody write Phillips service and tell them to have their China supplier use Locktite. I have no connection with Locktite. I&#x27;m just an Engineer. Actually using a screw for this ap is totally STUPID.Lots of ways to do this at half the manufacturing cost. I think an ex GM engineer designed this part. At least it sure looks like their work. Did marketing do this on purpose to sell more units? ? Hmmm.</li>

I&#x27;ve tried holding the brush differently, but it&#x27;s not comfortable.  The button should be disabled while the brush is in operation, if not moved to a different location on the handle.      I&#x27;ve also dinged the product one star for what I feel is sham marketing by Philips.  When I first purchased my Sonicare elite several years ago, they said to replace the heads every 6 months.  Then at some point, all of a sudden, they&#x27;re telling you to replace them every three months.  Has the workmanship gotten that shoddy?  Has some major study come out telling everyone to replace their brush every three months?  No, it&#x27;s just a ploy to sell more brushes, I imagine the margins are *very* high on the replacement heads. I doubt they cost more than a dollar to manufacture.  (To be fair, I doubt Philips is the only one who has done this -- Arm &amp; Hammer does it on their baking soda boxes as well, now you&#x27;re supposed to put a new box in the fridge every 30 days -- used to be every 90 days.  Ugh.)  But in any event, I&#x27;m not falling for this, and I feel the companies should be held accountable.  Somy part is to lower the rating by one star...</li>

The main unit has a rubberized handle grip to help you hold onto it with wet hands so it won&#x27;t slip.  And a 2-year warranty is nice.  Hopefully it&#x27;ll last much longer than that!     <li> The Sonicare is much superior to the Oral-B we phased out.  The Oral-B&#x27;s \\&quot;action\\&quot; was increasingly useless, perhaps because the replacement brush heads were becoming poorer in quality over time.  The Sonicare has a very vigorous, and seemingly very effective, brushing action (the next visit to the dental hygienist will tell the tale).  There is a bit of a hazard, though, in using this machine.  The brush head does move in a very energetic way, and it is made of hard plastic.  When the back of the brush rattles against the other teeth (the ones opposite of the ones you&#x27;re brushing), it is not merely an annoyance, it can chip a crown.  This goes from annoying to expensive in the blink of an eye.  Philips has not taken the design responsibility to put a soft rubber/plastic on the back of the brush head, so you will have to take care on your own.  Another design shortfall is that there are two buttons on the handle of this model: one for on/off; one for \\&quot;mode.\\&quot;  The mode button is actually more readily accessible than the on/off.  As a result, when you are brushing you will often inadvertently change the mode.  Nothing but an annoyance, not nearly at the level of the chipped-crown thing, but it is something that should have been seen to in the design stage.</li>

    <li> Sonicare Flexcare: The Perfect Toothbrush?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;About six months ago I decided it was about time to upgrade my toothbrush. It had treated me well, but the battery was no longer holding a charge for more than 60 seconds, and the heads were getting harder and harder to track down. Using Google and Amazon, I was quickly able to determine that the heavy hitters in the power toothbrush playing field were the Sonicare Flexcare and the Oral-B Triumph.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Flexcare is Sonicare&#x27;s flag-ship model. Earning its moniker from the multiple cleaning modes feature, this lithium battery powered device is the Mercedes of electric toothbrushes.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Alternatively, the Triumph is Oral-B&#x27;s \\&quot;Most technologically advanced toothbrush.\\&quot; It&#x27;s claim to fame is what Oral-B calls SmartGuide technology. Wirelessly, it transmits brushing feedback data (pressure, time, etc.) to an LCD screen. A bit over the top? Perhaps.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Both models offered top-of-the-line features and each had earned near 5-star reviews on Amazon. After reading through some of the reviews and pricing out each model I decided to take one last step before making my final decision: ask my dentist what they recommended. To my surprise they didn&#x27;t have a preference. I was instructed that either model would work great, so long as I brushed at least twice daily and flossed nightly!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I ended up purchasing the two-handle Sonicare Flexcare bundle with UV sanitizer. One handle for me, one for my girlfriend, and a super cool UV sanitization chamber to play with! Aside from the two handles (handle is really just Sonicare lingo for toothbrush) the box also contained: two travel pouches, one travel charger, and different color rings used to personalize each toothbrush. The colored rings certainly come in handy when two people living in the same household use the same model toothbrush!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Here are my thoughts after six months:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Build Quality:&lt;br /&gt;Excellent. The Flexcare feels very solid in-hand. The buttons are all sealed, easy to press, and the head slides on and off with little effort. The charging station is fairly compact and interfaces well with the handle.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Ease of Use:&lt;br /&gt;Pressing the mode select button will move through all available brush modes. Including: quick care, max care, massage, clean, and sensitive. Press the power button (with the toothbrush in your mouth!) and the Flexcare goes to work. After about 30 seconds or so the head will vibrate on and off a few times, this is a signal to move on to another section of your mouth. Sonicare calls this feature \\&quot;Quadpacer\\&quot; and claims it helps promote even cleaning. After two to three minutes the brush shuts itself off and you are done.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;What I like:&lt;br /&gt;-Keeps you honest. Turn the toothbrush off before the brushing cycle ends and you are only cheating yourself out of a thorough cleaning.&lt;br /&gt;-Multiple cycles. I tend to use the quick care (one minute) cycle in the mornings and in the evening I switch off between the normal clean cycle (two minutes) and the \\&quot;Max Care\\&quot; cycle (three minutes).&lt;br /&gt;-Newly designed head. Made to resist toothpaste build-up, it is easily removed for cleaning/sanitizing. The included heads are also very soft and extremely comfortable to brush with&lt;br /&gt;-Battery life is amazing. We&#x27;re talking upwards of two weeks used 2 to 3 times daily.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;What I don&#x27;t like:&lt;br /&gt;-Splatter! Don&#x27;t think about taking this thing out of your mouth while it is on, if you do micro droplets of toothpaste will go everywhere.&lt;br /&gt;-Cost. Price is high, but then again you can&#x27;t really put a price on healthy teeth and gums.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Conclusion:&lt;br /&gt;What really triggered me to write this review is how pleased I have been with this toothbrush over the past six months. Yes, three minutes feels like an eternity when brushing your teeth, but fire up your cell phone and read news/twitter updates/email/etc. and will go by in no time - the beauty of multitasking! What does my dentist think? At my last cleaning I was told my brushing could not have been better. No plaque, no tartar, and most importantly, no cavities. I wholeheartedly believe if everyone brushed with a toothbrush like this, dentists would lose a great deal of business! Hats off to Sonicare for making an excellent product that needs no improvement. I opted for massage where the brush cleans for thirty seconds and then massages for fifteen seconds of each part of the cycle (there being fours parts in total, outside top teeth, inside top teeth, outside bottom teeth and inside bottom teeth. It&#x27;s more a high whine than anything else and not that excessive. I found it tickled my palette almost unbearably the first few times, which has eased a little, and I&#x27;m sure this won&#x27;t be so bad once I get used to the unique and ticklish sensations. I&#x27;ve had my brushes over a year now and still am using the origianl lamp.  You get two indications that it is working, a flashing led above which goes steady once the process is finished and the chamber has not been opened (then it goes out) - plus the philips logo lights up from the UV inside but blocks the harmful rays from escaping by flourescing in the UV glow of the lamp.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This is a good system for children, as it has reminder buzzes on when to move on to the next set of teeth, and has 5 different cycles from gentile to vigorous.  My dentist recommended it to me, and I recommend it to anyone who doesnt&#x27;t want to see their dentist as often!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Positives:  It charges using an induction charger - meaning there are no exposed wires.  A coil hides behind the charging station and a second coil is inside the toothbrush.  When they are in close proximity (2\\&quot;) they couple energy from the AC line to the brush under charge.  This is a safe method of charging and does not require cords to plug into the brush.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Negatives:  The system has one li-ion battery.  Once it expires, philips provides a mechanism to use a screwdriver to remove the battery before throwing away the toothbrush, thus guaranteeing you will buy another one.  It would have been as easy to put a cap on the bottom allowing you to replace the expired battery at that time and then continue to use the brush electronics, which are very robust.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Of all power toothbrushes, this is the most efficient and professional.  It&#x27;s like comparing the new front load washing machines to yesteryear&#x27;s top load models in efficiency and economics.t.    Of all power toothbrushes, this is the most efficient and professional.  It&#x27;s like comparing the new front load washing machines to yesteryear&#x27;s top load models in efficiency and economics.</li>

    <li> I&#x27;ve been using this toothbrush for about 1-2 weeks and can already feel and see a difference. The brush heads are nice, although I prefer the larger one (standard vs. compact) to cover more tooth area. I have no problems fitting the sonic brush-head into my mouth, the extended reach is long enough to reach all the way to the back teeth and to clean the inside and outside of the teeth and along the gumline without having to open my mouth too wide. It is a very comfortable brushing experience overall. The vibration in the handle and brush head is also quite minimal for a sonic toothbrush, and I do not find it uncomfortable at all. The handle is also long, slim and easy to hold and maneuver. The on/off and mode buttons are easy to use and understand. The charger with UV sanitizer is also quite slim and fits onto my sink/countertop without taking up much room at all. The unit, overall, is really quite attractive. The UV sanitizer works wonderfully and accomodates 2 brush heads a time. I use my brush, then easily remove the brush head from the brush and put it in the sanitizer, close the door and hit the on/off button.     <li> I&#x27;m someone who&#x27;s always taken pretty good care of my teeth, and am proud of a life-long record of (almost) no cavities. Lately, when I go to the dentist, however, the dental hygienist always keeps mentioning these Philips toothbrushes. Last time I went in for my biannual cleaning, I asked: \\&quot;so what&#x27;s the deal with these brushes.\\&quot; She explained that they&#x27;re not like the little cheapie battery-operated toothbrushes you can buy in the grocery store right next to the regular Oral-Bs and Reach toothbrushes. And she said they can simply get your teeth cleaner than even the most experienced and dedicated manual brushing.    I was skeptical, but thought I&#x27;d give it a whirl. Man, was she right. The Philips Sonicare (FlexCare) is unlike anything else you&#x27;re likely to have used. In fact, it can be a bit intimidating the first time you put it inside your mouth, because the motor is so much more powerful than what you were probably expecting if you&#x27;ve previously used the kind of \\&quot;electric toothbrush\\&quot; you get at the store and have to put a AA battery into. Don&#x27;t worry, though: you won&#x27;t hurt yourself or take the enamel off your teeth. The removable, replaceable brush heads themselves come with bristles which are actually nice and soft - just like your dentist would likely recommend. It&#x27;s the motor action which is powerful. You control how hard you push down on your teeth, though - and you don&#x27;t need to push hard at all to get the full effect of the brush.    The two settings I use most often are the \\&quot;Go Care\\&quot; and \\&quot;Max Care\\&quot; settings; with these, the brush actually times you, allowing you to brush one each of four areas of your teeth (top front, top inside, bottom front and bottom inside) at a time. At the end of the time frame, the brush switches to a shorter \\&quot;gum massage\\&quot; action, then finally, there is a tone which is your cue to switch to a different area of your teeth, and the cycle begins again. After four of these (one for each of those four areas), the brush shuts itself off. You can also push the off button at any time (say, for instance, if you have to spit or speak with someone), and when you push on again, the brush will pick up right where it left off.    And the clean? Like nothing else you&#x27;ve experienced, except possibly the feeling you get right after you leave the dentist&#x27;s office after a cleaning. Well, you don&#x27;t get that \\&quot;scraped\\&quot; feeling, but that&#x27;s because there&#x27;s no scraping involved. But you DO get a feeling of clean that&#x27;s unlike anything you&#x27;ve likely experienced previously. On top of all that, the small UV chamber in which you store your brush-head during the day is an excellent idea. I&#x27;m not really sure just how much \\&quot;gunk\\&quot; would be on a regular toothbrush after a month or two of use, so I can&#x27;t give a measurable opinion as to how good a job the UV light is doing at killing potential bacteria. But it certainly can&#x27;t hurt, and if nothing else, the chamber provides a dust-free environment for the brush head, instead of just sitting in the medicine cabinet or in a toothbrush holder where it gathers dust all day.     All in all, the Philips FlexCare is a remarkable product, very well-built and well-thought out. You won&#x27;t be disappointed.</li>

Starting with the bottom teeth, I gently moved the brush head in the back and forth motion as directed.  It tingled with a sensation that was strange and a little uncomfortable.  After 45 seconds of \\&quot;clean\\&quot; and \\&quot;massage\\&quot;, the Quadpacer signal indicated it was time for a change of location, as it did faithfully three more times.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Observations:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1.     <li> I bought this toothbrush for $40 from craigslist a couple months ago after hearing from friends how great electronic toothbrushes were. I started using it on a regular basis and at first it was great. I just charged it up every 2 weeks and it helped to clean those hard to reach areas like the back of your teeth and molars.     But after about a months use the blue line on the toothbrush head already begun to recede indicating that I would soon need a new toothbrush head. So I starting looking on the internet and to my shock and dismay I found out that a pack of 3 replacement heads costs anywhere from $23-30. If you do the math that&#x27;s $7.50-10.00 per replacement head. At first, you may not even bat an eye at this price and assume that the price is somehow justified by the technology in the toothbrush head, but when you take a close look at the toothbrush head you&#x27;ll see that the head has no moving parts and that it&#x27;s the handle that simply vibrates. What&#x27;s more is that the head uses probably 30-40% less material and plastic than a regular toothbrush which on average costs $2-3. So can someone please explain why something that should logically cost less since it uses less materials and uses NO radical new technology in fact costs 300%-400% more than a conventional toothbrush and why you would pay for such an overpriced product? Is there anything to justify the ridiculous cost of these replacement heads? Also if they were going to charge me $10 per replacement head I would expect to last at least 6 months-1 year but if you read the product manual, they suggest that you replace it every 3 months so you&#x27;ll end up doling out $40 per year just for the toothbrush heads.    Another issue that irked me is that when you look at the toothbrush handle and read the instruction manual you&#x27;ll realize that it is run by a rechargeable lithium ion battery. As we all know, rechargeable batteries slowly lose their charging capacity throughout the life of its use (it&#x27;s called memory loss). A point that may not be as obvious is that this toothbrush is meant to slowly die out or be unusable within approximately 2 years. How do I know that? Look at the manufacturers warranty on the product; Its covered under warranty for only 2 years.     So lets say that your toothbrush finally dies after 2 years due to a worn out battery. So an economical and logical person would find out how much it would cost to buy a replacement battery and replace it instead of dropping another $120 on a brand new toothbrush. You&#x27;d find out that you can buy a replacement rechargeable lithium ion battery for this toothbrush for about $5. So when you go to replace the battery in the toothbrush you would think you just unscrew the bottom, pop out the old battery and pop in the new one. WRONG! They&#x27;ve made this product so that if you try to replace the battery by removing battery compartment from the body of the toothbrush it destroys the circuitry of the toothbrush rendering it broken and unusable. This is called PLANNED OBSOLESCENCE which means that Philips intentionally made these toothbrushes in such a way that they will mostly break down within 2 years so that you&#x27;re likely to drop another $120+ every 2 years to buy another one of these overpriced vibrators. If you want more info on planned obsolescence take a look at this short clip: [...]    Now I know a lot of you are probably thinking &#x27;Well I&#x27;ve had my electric toothbrush for 10 years and it still works fine&#x27;. Yes, there&#x27;s always going to be an exception, but you have to realize a simple fact which is that the sole interest of these large corporations be it Philips who manufactures this toothbrush, General Motors or Apple is PROFIT. This means that they will intentionally produce products that are specifically designed to break down or be unusable/incompatible within a specific time frame so that you buy their products over and over again thereby taking more of your money and increasing their profits. If you seriously thinkthat these corporations sit down and try to figure out how to produce the most efficient and durable product and thereby have your financial interest at hand, you need a serious reality check.     So what can you do to discourage planned obsolescence and not be subject to these low quality and overpriced products? It&#x27;s actually quite simple; DON&#x27;T BUY THEIR PRODUCTS! You have to realize that every time you purchase something whether it be an organic apple as opposed to a pesticide sprayed apple or a T-shirt made in the USA as opposed to a sweatshop in China, you have a direct impact on these corporations profits and that you have the ability to influence their future decisions. You are the lifeline of these corporations and they depend on you, the consumer, to buy their products in order to succeed and profit. If we all collectively stop buying their products then I can assure you they&#x27;ll start to listen and begin producing the types of high quality products that we demand.</li>

    <li> I had been using the Sonicare Advance for the past 4 years. I see some nice improvements over that model.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;- Gunk doesn&#x27;t build up anymore. Had I known about this sooner, I would have upgraded sooner.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My only gripe (for which I am deducting a star) is the placement of the power on/off button. This is the green button that you see on the toothbrush. It&#x27;s positioned to easily turn on the tooth brush since it&#x27;s where your thumb would naturally rest. But this also makes it very easy to accidentally turn off when you are moving the toothbrush around and twisting your wrist. If tend to do other things when you brush your teeth, you might not notice the toothbrush turning off and will be depriving yourself of the recommended 2 minutes of brushing.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;UPDATE (3/11/09): I would deduct an additional star if this were possible here. I had a nasty case of mold on the base. I hadn&#x27;t used the UV sanitizer in a while, so the sanitizer door was closed for a few weeks. You really need to use a towel to dry off the toothbrush before placing it back on the base. Programming the brush for the mode that you like every time you pick it up is not hard, but it&#x27;s really annoying.  Sonicare: please fix this in later models.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This brush comes with 2 chargers, one for home (with the sanitizer) and a travel one (without a sanitizer.) On my Oral-B I had to remove the brush head to wash out the gunk after brushing, but because the Sonicare brush heads are longer, very, very litle gunk gets in them.  That was a pleasant surprise.  Although, removing and attaching the brush head on the Flexcare wand requires a lot more force, which I don&#x27;t like.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The U.V. sanitizer is a nice gadget, but who knows how useful it really is?  In fact, there may even be some long-term immune system dangers by killing every bacteria/virus in sight, just like using anti-bacterial soap, but this is not the forum for that.  I used the UV Sanitizer a few times, but I don&#x27;t use it at all anymore because of what I believe to be a very real problem with all the anti-bacterial products out there these days.  Although, based on the few times I did use it, I could see where its utilization on a daily basis would be cumbersome.  If you brush twice a day, it becomes too much of a bother to remove the brush head every time and put it in the sanitizer.  The brush head needs to be aligned perfectly in the sanitizer and the door closed and snapped gently.  If you have big hands, putting the brush head into the sanitizer is more awkward, especially if you&#x27;re using the large brush head (FYI: the brush heads come in 2 sizes, small and large, and one of each is included in the package.)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It&#x27;s nice to see that Sonicare has FINALLY ditched the NiCad batteries and went to Li-ion batteries; what took so long?  This change means that the brush will now run longer on a single charge, and won&#x27;t develop a memory by leaving it on the charging stand.  It&#x27;s also the reason that the brush handle is now smaller which makes it more manageable.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As much as I love this brush, I do realize that the price Sonicare has marketed it at is exceedingly high.  If I were to buy it again, I would save $20 and get the one without the U.V. sanitizer.  Other than the high price and a little nitpicking on the brushing modes, I really couldn&#x27;t be more pleased with this brush. I can&#x27;t understand one reviewer who said the brush doesn&#x27;t sit right or balance well on the stand.     <li> I bought this toothbrush following a recommendation from a dental hygienist, who only said two words: \\&quot;Philips\\&quot; and \\&quot;sonic.\\&quot; So I was on my own trying to winnow down the wide array of models and features available online and at local retail stores.  I settled on this unit based on several positive reviews, its feature set, and the fact that for $5 more than the next model down, it came with the UV sanitizer feature.  Although that is an unnecessary embellishment, I thought what can it hurt to try it out for about 3% more money?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have now been using the Sonicare Flexcare for more than 90 days, and I have to say I am extremely pleased at its performance so far.  The sonic action really does leave my teeth and gumline feeling cleaner than I was EVER able to get them by manual brushing, and I have even seen slight improvement in my periodontal situation (some moderately deep pockets).  Of course I did start with a pair of very thorough periodontal cleanings 3 months apart, but my periodontist and hygienists agree than the Sonicare is an outstanding dental home-care maintenance tool.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The features on this unit all work as advertised, and are actually handy.  I found the 14-use \\&quot;ramp-up\\&quot;, which slowly increases the brushing to full-power over about a week&#x27;s time, to be a good way to ease into the Sonicare experience, which can be startling for a newbie. This is a very powerful cleaning tool, unlike anything I have ever felt, other than at the dentist&#x27;s office.  I normally use the \\&quot;MaxCare\\&quot; cycle, 30 seconds of cleaning plus 15 seconds of massage on each quadrant.  The regular \\&quot;Clean\\&quot; cycle (30 seconds of cleaning per quadrant) is fine for the morning brushing.  The \\&quot;GoCare\\&quot; cycle (15 seconds of cleaning per quadrant) is fine if you&#x27;re in a hurry, or just want to touch up The \\&quot;Sensitive\\&quot; cycle will probably come in handy as I ease back into brushing following any future dental work or periodontal surgery. The \\&quot;Massage\\&quot; cycle is fine for some gum stimulation.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I find the feature that makes the toothbrush \\&quot;burp\\&quot;, a tiny pause and beep after each of the first three segments of a cycle, to be also extremely handy.  I don&#x27;t have to keep track of time, I just switch to the next quadrant when the toothbrush tells me to.  The brush heads fit perfectly, and do not seem to get any gunk underneath where they attach to the unit. I do take the brush head off and clean the mounting post about once every 8-10 days.  The battery seems excellent: the instructions say a full charge takes 24 hours, so when the battery indicator has been on one green bar (out of three) for a couple days, I put the unit on the charger after my evening usage, and leave it there for 24 hours, using a manual brush the next morning.  The charge has lasted at least 10 days per, so far, or at least 20 cycles.  It might even go longer, but it&#x27;s probably bad for the battery to drain it all the way. BTW, I do NOT keep the unit on the charger, but stand it up next to it. I believe it is better for the battery to \\&quot;cycle\\&quot; all the way up and most of the way down, rather than keep it fully charged all the time. Your experience and intuition may vary.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I use the sanitizer about once a week, putting the brush head in the little compartment after the evening brushing, firing up the UV light, and then wiping off the unit&#x27;s mounting post. The sanitizing cycle takes only 10-15 minutes, and shuts itself off automagically. So far, I have avoided any hideous mouth diseases (except for my pre-existing periodontal disease), but I didn&#x27;t contract any in my previous 55 years of non-sanitized toothbrush use, so I can&#x27;t say this UV sanitizing thing is too essential. Might be good if you shared the brush AND the brush head. (Yuck-o!)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I was able to buy extra brush heads for about $8.50 apiece for a 3-pack, cheaper than retail.  Philips also sent me one free one as a purchase bonus for signing up online with them. You&#x27;re supposed to change the brushhead every 90 days, but you can probably go 4-6 months between new heads without diminishing brushing effectiveness too much.  Since you actually do NOT need to press the brush hard against the tooth and gumline surfaces, the brush does not wear out and get ragged as quickly as a manual brush.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Regarding criticisms that this toothbrush spurts toothpaste and water all over, is difficult to use, make a deafening sound, is accidentally activated, etc, I can only say that some people clearly did not read the instructions carefully.  I have found NONE of these flaws and, if used correctly, the unit is fairly easy to use.  It should be held lightly but firmly, not clenched in one&#x27;s fist, taking care to keep your fingers off the various buttons on the front.  No \\&quot;brushing\\&quot; motion is required: simply moving the buzzing brush head over the tooth surface and gumline at about a 45 degree angle does the trick.  My teeth feel cleaner than they have ever felt, and seem to stay that way between professional cleanings. I have also noticed an appreciable increase in the overall \\&quot;whiteness\\&quot; of my smile, an unexpected benefit.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I cannot speak to the longevity of this product, but the two-year warranty should take care of any issues.  If it breaks in month 25 of my ownership, I will definitely buy another one- it&#x27;s still cheaper than dental work!  To possibly improve my chances for toothbrush longevity, I rinse the brush head and toothbrush body briefly under running water after usage, dry it lightly with a hand towel, and flick it a few times to shake the excess water off the brush head. So far, I am VERY pleased with this product, and recommend it unconditionally to anyone seeking to maintain and augment their professional dental care.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;SEMI-DISCLAIMER:  My dad is a retired dentist (practiced 45 years) and had nothing to say about, or add to, this review.  I showed him the toothbrush, he felt the buzzing brush head with his finger, and said, \\&quot;Huh.  Might have to get one.\\&quot;head every 90 days, but you can probably go 4-6 months between new heads without diminishing brushing effectiveness too much.     <li> My original Sonicare toothbrush just gave up the ghost after just under a decade of use.     <li> I&#x27;ve been using an older Sonicare model, the \\&quot;Essence 5300\\&quot; on which the switch was beginning to go out.  I decided to upgrade to a Flexcare model and am very glad I did.  The Flexcare has been a great improvement all around.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Pros:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;-New Lighter, Slimmer Handle&lt;br /&gt;This is probably the first thing you&#x27;ll notice if you&#x27;re coming from an older Sonicare handle, and it is a very welcome improvement.  The FlexCare handle is small and feels much better in the hand than my old bulky 5300 handle.  The unit is actually longer than my old brush, but that&#x27;s not a big deal at all.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;-New ProResults Brush Head system&lt;br /&gt;The new heads are great.  Sonicare moved the tuning fork from the head to the handle, which means smaller brush heads than on the old models.  A 3 pack of the new heads is the same price as a 2 pack of the old heads, making them actually a better deal for a superior product.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;-No More Crud in the Handle!&lt;br /&gt;The biggest problem with my old brush was that old toothpaste/drool/water tended to collected in the space where the handle connects to the brush head.  It would get all moldy and gross if you didn&#x27;t clean it out regularly.  Thankfully, this problem is completely gone with the Flexcare handles.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;-Lithium Ion Batteries&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;ve waited a long time for Sonicare to upgrade from inferior NiCd batteries, and they finally have.  With Lithium Ion, you don&#x27;t have to worry about battery capacity decreasing over time, or a memory effect.  The new batteries charge faster, too.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;-UV Sanitizer Included&lt;br /&gt;UV Sanitizers for toothbrushes are relatively new to the market, and a great idea.  I always felt a little gross letting my brush sit out on the counter, even with the cover that comes with sonicare heads, and then putting it in my mouth.  Scientists actually recommend that a toothbrush be kept 3 feet from the toilet due to \\&quot;airborne particles\\&quot; from the flush - yuck!  A UV sanitizer will kill anything that might land on your brush, as well as things such as cold germs that might have come from your own mouth.  Using the sanitizer is easy, just pop the brush head(s) in, press the green button, and wait for the UV light to kill the germs.  I store my brush head inside the sanitizer until I need it next.  The Charger is integrated with the sanitizer, although a separate travel charger is included.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;-Quadpacer&lt;br /&gt;This is basically a beep that goes off every 30 seconds while brushing, reminding you to switch to a new area of your mouth.  It has appeared in previous models (not my 5300 though), and is nice if you&#x27;ll use it, but I tend to go at my own pace as I focus more on problem areas in my mouth and less on others.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;-5 Total Brushing Modes/Routines&lt;br /&gt;There are 3 selectable \\&quot;modes\\&quot;: clean mode: (2 minutes broken into 30 second segments), sensitive (a \\&quot;gentler\\&quot; clean mode) and massage (the brush pulsates for gum stimulation).  Go Care Routine shortines the standard 2 minute clean mode to 1 minute, while Max Care is a longer, 3 minute cycle that includes both clean and massage mode.  I set the brush on clean mode and tend not to use the other options, but some may find them useful.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;-More Environmentally Friendly&lt;br /&gt;Although buying a new product of any sort will always have a negative environmental footprint, these new brushes are better than the old models due to their Li-Ion batteries, reduced bulk, and lower waste in the smaller replacement brush heads.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cons:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;-Price&lt;br /&gt;Let&#x27;s be clear on this: a Sonicare toothbrush is a luxury product.  You&#x27;re paying a lot more up front, and you get to keep paying more every time you buy replacement heads.  Surprisingly, heads for Flexcare units are actually a cheaper than the older models; you get 3 Flexcare heads for the same price as 2 of the old heads.  The per head price is still several times what it would cost to buy a new manual brush; but for me the superior cleaningis worth it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Noise&lt;br /&gt;-Flexcare models are louder than older models.  I&#x27;m not sure why this is, and supposedly vibration has been reduced in exchange, but the noise can be too much for some.  The UV sanitizer also makes a quiet electric \\&quot;hum\\&quot; when plugged in with the door closed, even if the UV bulb isn&#x27;t run.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;-Buttons can be depressed while brushing&lt;br /&gt;A couple of people have complained about accidentally hitting 1 of the 2 buttons on the handle while brushing.  It hasn&#x27;t happened to me, but for completeness I&#x27;ll include this as a possible con.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This brush is a vast improvement over my previous brush, and has fixed most of the problems I had without introducing any significant new ones.  The fact that replacement brush heads are actually cheaper than on my old brush is a big plus.  I highly recommend the Flexcare brushes as a great upgrade to any toothbrush, electric or manual, that you&#x27;re currently using.has been reduced in exchange, but the noise can be too much for some.  The UV sanitizer also makes a quiet electric \\&quot;hum\\&quot; when plugged in with the door closed, even if the UV bulb isn&#x27;t run.    -Buttons can be depressed while brushing  A couple of people have complained about accidentally hitting 1 of the 2 buttons on the handle while brushing.  It hasn&#x27;t happened to me, but for completeness I&#x27;ll include this as a possible con.    Overall:    This brush is a vast improvement over my previous brush, and has fixed most of the problems I had without introducing any significant new ones.  The fact that replacement brush heads are actually cheaper than on my old brush is a big plus.  I highly recommend the Flexcare brushes as a great upgrade to any toothbrush, electric or manual, that you&#x27;re currently using.</li>

    <li> At my last dental checkup, the dentist said I had early gum disease and needed deep scaling/planing. My hygienist, who did the scaling, recommended I start using a Sonicare FlexCare Plus. After shopping around, I opted for the plain FlexCare model, because it has all the same functions as the Plus--they&#x27;re just labelled differently. Also, at Amazon I was able to get this model with the UV brush sanitizer.  I was skeptical about spending so much money for a toothbrush, but the positive reviews, plus my disdain for periodontist visits, convinced me to try it. Upon arrival, I charged it for 24 hours before using it, during which time I thoroughly read the instructions. I suggest any buyer do the same, as this thing has a lot of settings and options.   Once I started brushing with it, I couldn&#x27;t believe the difference in how my teeth feel after using the FlexCare. I use the standard cleaning cycle, two minutes with a pause and beep every 30 seconds to tell you when to move to the next quadrant. My teeth feel noticeably cleaner and smoother after brushing with the FlexCare, pretty much like when you get them cleaned at the dentist. Can&#x27;t tell much difference with my gums, but given its speed when it&#x27;s operating, it obviously does as advertised--forces the toothpaste/water solution between your teeth and under your gum line to completely clean all the places you can&#x27;t get with a normal brush.  The FlexCare comes with two brush heads. The shorter one has a concave bristle surface; the longer one has a double-concave surface and has a larger set of bristles, and is supposed to do a more through cleaning job. I use that one; the smaller one seems better suited for a child.  The handle unit seems well made and carefully sealed against moisture. The weight is about perfect--just heavy enough to keep it stable when it&#x27;s running, but not too heavy to maneuver and hold for several minutes. It&#x27;s also well balanced.  At first, the controls and LED indicators on the brush handle seem confusing--but I&#x27;ve brushed manually for the last couple decades, so that&#x27;s likely just me. The power button is logically placed just under your thumb, and all you really need to do is turn it on and brush. The unit shuts off automatically. The only time you have to push another button is when you&#x27;re changing brushing cycles.  The handle comes set by default to the two-minute clean cycle, the 30-second beep cycle, and the startup mode--this uses a slower brush rate to start, and gradually increases over the first two weeks to the full speed. You can change the cycle with the handle controls, and the other defaults can be reset while the unit is in the charging stand. There&#x27;s a quick clean cycle and a gentle setting for those with sensitive teeth.  The two-week startup mode is a great feature, because this brush takes some getting used to. It vibrates so fast that it startles you unpleasantly if you touch the plastic shaft of the brush tip to your teeth while it&#x27;s running--which is easy to do. It took me a few brushes to get used to shifting directions without inadvertently rattling my teeth.  The FlexCare comes with a soft travel case and a separate travel charger--that&#x27;s a nice touch. They also include a set of three alternate snap-on color rings so multiple family members can easily identify their own brush tip. One thing it doesn&#x27;t have is a separate base or stand for the handle. Our bathroom counter space is limited, so I have the charger/cleaner on a shelf unit separate from our vanity. It&#x27;d be nice to have a small base that would hold the brush upright, rather than tossing it in a drawer or letting it lay on the counter. I don&#x27;t want to keep it in the charger all the time anyway, as it&#x27;s usually better to completely drain a rechargeable battery before recharging. But that&#x27;s a minor gripe.  The only real negative I can see is the cost of replacement brush tips--around $20 for a pack of 3. That can get pricey if more than two people use it. Each tips is supposed to last about three months. There&#x27;s a $5 coupon for these in the FlexCare box, and your dentist probably has the coupons available.   Overall, the FlexCare is worth the money--especially at Amazon&#x27;s price. It&#x27;s made well, comes well-equipped, has a lot of settings to choose from, and most important, it seems certain to do a great job keeping your teeth and gums healthy.</li>

And indeed, it took what was basically tar off my teeth, but it made my teeth, gums and tounge numb when I was finished.  I brushed for about 60 seconds (using a clock with a second hand to make sure I did 15 seconds in each quarter of my mouth) just to be sure I was following the recommended useage for this first time.  I almost returned it right then and there because of how numb my mouth became.  To understand why I didn&#x27;t, you&#x27;ll have to know a little about my mouth:  My dentist says that I have a plaque problem. I go once a year, I brush twice a day, and I floss every few days.  I have never walked away from a dental cleaning (even a \\&quot;full mouth debridement\\&quot; that I had a few years back which took an hour) without being able to still feel ridges at the edge of my teeth where there was still plaque built up (that&#x27;s right folks, I can feel my plaque with my tounge because it is so hardened on).  Ok, back to my story.  As I put the toothbrush head in the UV sanitizer and replaced the handle on the counter, I noticed that I couldn&#x27;t feel any plaque!  In one minute this has done more than any toothbrush I&#x27;ve ever owned, more than flossing, more than a full hour of horrible deep cleaning by a dental hygenist, more than four different dentists (and perhaps more when I was younger) could do.  This took all of my plaque away!  I have a cleaning in a few weeks, I&#x27;ll try to remember to update this after the cleaning to tell you what my dentist has to say.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So why four stars?  Well, for two weeks my mouth felt numb after each use, which would have dropped my rating to two stars when balanced with the excellent results.  But after two weeks that started to fade and now I only feel a little tingle.  So I bumped it up to four stars because if you stick with it you&#x27;ll get used to it and not feel it as much.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;What other features does it have?  Well, the UV sanitizer was a great deal for me because I have always used one with my regular toothbrushes and I would have had to get one to fit whatever brush I got.  The sanitizer works great and I give it five stars without complaint.  The only thing I can&#x27;t comment on is its longevity, since I have had the cheaper ones break a lot, but hopefully this one is made well and will last long.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Then there is the charging base.  This uses a new technology that I read about last year after CES which send electricity to the device just from being within less than an inch of the base top.  Try it, hover above and it will charge!  This is not only cool, it also means no metal to corrode in your bathroom.  The travel charger works the same, but my complaint there is that a lack of weight will cause you to need to position the cord carefully when putting the travel charger down or you wont be able to use it.  Also, the travel case doesn&#x27;t hold the charger.  However, for short trips I&#x27;m going to bring a cheap disposable electric in a travel sanitizer so I don&#x27;t risk my expensive toothbrush so that isn&#x27;t a problem for me.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The \\&quot;deluxe\\&quot; travel case is a joke, being that it is made from canvas and very cheap, I give it two stars.  However, I didn&#x27;t expect much so I wasn&#x27;t dissapointed.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The brush head is smaller than I am use to.  This was annoying at first, but I got used to it.  If it was larger, it would be harder to fit into smaller curves around the gumline.  Since it does the brushing for me (I just move it slowly back and forth, less than 50 strokes does my whole mouth), this isn&#x27;t a problem at all now.  The pro brush head is also designed well and it cleans great.  I will continue to use that head.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Now for the two complaints that I have aside from my initial reaction of numbness:  First, the battery is one of those that you have to use up before you charge.  That isn&#x27;t a problem, except that they should have put a charge button on the charger because I have to store it next to the charger instead of on it when I don&#x27;t want it to charge.  The second complaint is that the programs (which I haven&#x27;t figured out yet) clear whenever you stop using it or if you don&#x27;t turn it on for three seconds.  This means that you have to find your setting, move the brush quickly to your mouth, and turn it on, all within 3 seconds.  And the next time you use it, the brush has reset to its default.  Apparently they put money into designing these program modes but they don&#x27;t want you to use them.  I just ignore them because of this.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;All in all, everyone needs this toothbrush!  I hope that dentists start to recommend it and readers start to buy it.     <li> Here are two things Phillips will not tell you about their Sonicare toothbrushes and heads.     1) The collar that holds the toothbrush to the handle will disintegrate in a couple of months. That&#x27;s what prompted this review, because they would not replace mine after it fell apart two weeks after purchasing a replacement.     They manufacturer these things to disintegrate so you will continue to buy replacements - planned obsolescence. However, I suspect their China supplier is skimping on the plastic specifications and they fall apart in weeks instead of months. (Do you think China would really do that?)    2) UNPLUG your base until you need to charge the toothbrush.  If you charge it up overnight, then unplug the base, the toothbrush will work for four brushings per day for about a month.  Then, when it signals or stops, plug the base in to charge it.     This method will allow your toothbrush to work for five years or longer. If you keep the base plugged in all the time, these NiCad batteries develop memory and will stop functioning after 18 to 24 months.    A bonus, if you travel a lot as I do, you don&#x27;t have to pack the charger.  Just make sure it&#x27;s topped off and you&#x27;re good for a month&#x27;s vacation.</li>

    <li> Have not had an electric toothbrush for about 10 years, but got the Sonicare after a dentist recommended.    Brush seems to clean better than manual brushing and you get used to the vibration etc.    A few quibbles:  Phillips should have the brush remember the last setting.  It resets to default \\&quot;Quick Clean\\&quot; 1 minute setting every time.    Don&#x27;t expect to hear the \\&quot;beep\\&quot; of the \\&quot;Quadpacer\\&quot;, (the timer that does 15 seconds per quadrant in Quick Clean mode, or 30 seconds in \\&quot;Max Clean\\&quot;) it really is just a pause.    The lithium battery is not replaceable.  Philips expects you to remove the battery for special disposal and toss the rest of the brush away, then buy a new one.   Since lithium batteries have a fixed life, the battery should be user-replaceable.  I expect that the brush will outlast the battery, so throwing it away is a waste.    Additional note 2/1/10.  Product quit working entirely in January 2010.  Phillips replaced it at no charge, even though it was well out of warranty.</li>
    <li> I know, I know, that much for a toothbrush? Really? The price is the biggest drawback to this toothbrush. But if you decide to take the plunge, let me tell you what you&#x27;re getting yourself into.     I&#x27;ve owned a sonicare for several years now, and I have always been impressed with the level of performance. I&#x27;m moving up from a sonicare advance, which is their base model. I was blown away by the difference between the advance and the flexcare. I knew it would be better, but not this much. In my review, I will compare it to the advance for a reference.     The Design: Compared to the advance, the design is much improved. The body is slimmer and therefore easier to maneuver around. The brush design was the best improvement. The advance uses a larger, more square shaped brush which makes it somewhat awkward to reach the teeth in the very back. The smaller, more rounded brush head on the flexcare makes it so easy to reach all of the teeth in my mouth. Also, the screw on brush head is gone. Yippee! The brush head now slides on and locks into place. With the screw on models, gunk and grime would build up underneath the threads which made me very queasy. I think my favorite improvement comes with the new design on the base charger. In the older models, the toothbrush would fit into the charger, so about an inch of the toothbrush was hidden while on the charger. This design inevitably lead to a build up of gunk on the bottom of the brush and on the inside of the charger unless you completely dried off the toothbrush before placing it into the charger base. This was very annoying and gross to look at. Philips redesigned the base with the flexcare. Now the base charger is completely flat with a little peg sticking up in the middle. The toothbrush has a complimentary  hole in the bottom for the peg to fit into. Now the toothbrush is completely exposed to the air so it dries out better. No more gunk!  Also, it would be pretty easy to share this toothbrush with someone else, assuming you have your own brush head :)    Performance/Features: Performance is great. Simple as that. My teeth feel dentist clean every time I use it. The brush has a couple different settings to fit your different moods, but the normal clean mode turns the brush on for two minutes, which is divided into 30 seconds for each quadrant. The brush signals each quadrant change by a split second interruption in the brushing action. I almost would have preferred a beep, but this works ok.     For the first 14 brush cycles, this unit ramps up on the intensity of the brush action. If you use a sonicare currently, you should have no problem adjusting to this. I didn&#x27;t notice any of the irritating tickling vibrations common on the sonicare brushes. If you&#x27;ve never used a sonicare, don&#x27;t worry too much. Everyone always becomes accustom to the vibrations, and after a few brush cycles you won&#x27;t even notice it anymore.     UV Sanitizer: It&#x27;s an interesting addition to the toothbrush. I can&#x27;t comment on how well it works since I don&#x27;t have the means to test that, but you simply detach the brush head and put it into the UV compartment for a 15(?) minute cleaning cycle. A toothbrush that cleans itself, nifty.      Overall this is a great toothbrush. If you&#x27;re unwilling to spend the big bucks for this model, and I certainly understand, I would suggest getting the flexcare without the sanitizer or go for the elite model. Heck, you can&#x27;t go wrong with any of the sonicare models, as they are all improvements over the manual sticks you have been using.</li>

While waiting for it to arrive, I went a week or two with just a manual toothbrush and I definitely felt the difference in terms of my overall oral health and \\&quot;freshness.\\&quot; (I am an efficient brusher manually, but it just does a better job. Then there&#x27;s GoCare (15 seconds each - good if you want to do a brief brushing after a meal or something), MaxCare (3 minutes, 45 seconds each - 30 seconds normal, 15 doing a pulse). If you are a regular flosser/good brusher, or you own an older Sonicare, you probably don&#x27;t want 14 days of gentle ramping up. One beep means you just disabled it, two beeps means you turned it back on.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Now, time for some pros and cons vs. the ancient advance I had:&lt;br /&gt;+This brush is much smaller and the rubber is more ergonomic.&lt;br /&gt;+The old brushes were bulkier too, the newer brushes are better. This probably goes without saying, but don&#x27;t submerge thehandle...&lt;br /&gt;+The charger base on the old Sonicare was also recessed. This comes with a travel charger, but no second handle, and only a soft case.&lt;br /&gt;-My dentist doubts the need for the UV cleaner and advises people to buy the FlexCare without it.     <li> Your Dentist is like your Mom and Dad:  really, they just want what&#x27;s best for you.  Of course, sometimes what&#x27;s best isn&#x27;t always what&#x27;s practical. The difference is that the head pulses and emits sonic waves that shake the microscopic ick that you&#x27;ve accumulated right off your teeth.  The vibration doesn&#x27;t rattle your head or make your eyes water:  it sounds like you&#x27;re gargling with a lightsaber, but the feeling amounts to a mild vibration that leaves your gums tingly.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The last time I had an electric toothbrush, it was heavier than the Sonicare, despite being much shorter. The Sonicare package I purchased here at Amazon came with:     - a small charger just slightly wider than the toothbrush  - a larger charging base with UV sanitizer (to kill stray bacteria accumulated on the head)  - the connector plug  - two heads for the brush  - a travel carrying case    All of it was packed into a relatively small box and the heads even have a plastic cap to slip over the bristles when you&#x27;re not using the toothbrush.     <li> I have been using Sonicare electric toothbrushes for many years. Otherwise, they were virtually indestructible.  Those who use the old design know what I&#x27;m talking about. Only time I had to replace them was when the sealed Ni-Cad battery died and failed to keep a charge, usually lasting about 5 years.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Then they took a page out of Oral-B&#x27;s playbook and changed and simplified the brush head design whereby they are inserted onto a metal post like the Oral-B design rather than screwed on. Now it is much easier to change and keep the brush head / inter-connect area clean. I also like the fact that they switched to lighter Li-Ion battery and the charge seems to last longer.  The brushing action also feels more powerful than the old design. The UV sanitizing chamber is bit gimmicky but at least the science behind it is sound. I love the Sonicare brushes in general.  The reason I deducted 3 stars is because with this particular model, I had 3 units fail prematurely in less than 2 years where the metal post retaining the brush head had come off the main body.  Once that happens, the water-tight seal is broken and the unit is rendered useless.  Being a dental care professional, when I called the Philips service center to address my concerns, their reply was perfunctory at best and only emphasized the fact that my warranty had expired.  Therefore, I&#x27;d be weary of recommending this particular model; I&#x27;m not certain if they improved or corrected this design weakness with FlexCare Plus.     <li> Our periodontist suggested that we purchase the Philips Sonicare FlexCare Rechargeable Sonic Toothbrush.  He said that an ordinary toothbrush could not possibly perform as well as this one.  When a person brushes manually, he does most of the work, but when operating a sonic toothbrush, the user must be careful to apply only apply light pressure, angle the brush so that it touches both the tooth and the gum, and move the brush slowly from tooth to tooth.  There will be a period of adjustment for the average person who is used to putting extra effort into cleaning his teeth.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Sonicare FlexCare has a clear and thorough instruction booklet explaining each feature.  The handle is comfortable, the on/off button is conveniently located, and there is a travel charger if you want to take the brush with you on the road.  A fully charged brush will work for two weeks, but you may leave the brush in the charger 24/7 without causing any damage.  For those who are nervous about germs, there is even a UV sanitizer to zap any bacteria that may have settled on the brush head.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you want to experiment with different brushing modes, there is a standard \\&quot;clean mode,\\&quot; a \\&quot;sensitive mode\\&quot; for a more gentle feel, and a \\&quot;massage mode\\&quot; for extra gum stimulation.  There are also short and longer brushing cycles and a \\&quot;Smartimer\\&quot; that automatically turns off the toothbrush at the end of a brushing cycle. If you want to put your money where your mouth is, this high tech item would be a sensible purchase.</li>

    <li> DEVICE INSTALL/SETUP&lt;br /&gt;The Philips Sonicare FlexCare Rechargeable Sonic Toothbrush required no complicated setup, simply removing the items from the packaging and plugging it in.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;MANUALS/DOCUMENTATION&lt;br /&gt;I was pleased to find that not only does this product come with very informative, concise written instructions, but the manuals can also be easily downloaded from the Philips&#x27; website in PDF format.  This is very handy for those of us who don&#x27;t always keep up as easily with the printed manuals, or who prefer to be able to text search the manual for the information we need.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;FUNCTIONALITY&lt;br /&gt;I have never used an electric toothbrush of any kind before, and although I&#x27;ve been intrigued by the idea for some time, I was a little nervous to use this one at first.  Turning the toothbrush on for the first time didn&#x27;t alleviate my nervousness much, as the device certainly SOUNDS powerful.  To my relief, actually using the toothbrush was painless, although the first few times it tickled a bit.  I have been using the toothbrush daily since September 21, 2007 and am happy to report that this product performs as advertised.  In fact, my teeth feel and look as good as if I&#x27;ve just had them cleaned at the dentist&#x27;s office.  I&#x27;m brushing in half the time I did manually, and the Philips Sonicare FlexCare Rechargeable Sonic Toothbrush is doing twice as good a job as I ever did with a standard toothbrush.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The toothbrush is packaged with a number of items, including a travel case and a travel charger which packs in a toiletry bag much easier than the countertop charger with the built in sanitizer.  Also included is two toothbrush heads, a compact size and a full size.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I use the sanitizer faithfully each time I brush my teeth, but to be perfectly honest, I don&#x27;t know how to judge whether the sanitizer is really making any difference or not.  I love the idea of it, and I hope that it is truly keeping my toothbrush germ-free.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I particularly love the massaging function on the toothbrush, designed to prevent gingivitis by massaging the gums.  With just over two weeks of regular use, I can already tell a difference here.  Using the massager stimulates the gums, making them stronger and healthier.  The cleaning routine I prefer, the &#x60;MaxCare&#x27;, includes massage in the routine for each tooth quadrant, making it easy to incorporate into your daily brush habit without extra effort.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Speaking of the cleaning routines, there are two:  MaxCare, and GoCare.  I&#x27;ve tested the one-minute GoCare routine and found it acceptable for a rush job, but I much prefer to perform the full MaxCare routine, which runs through a 4-quadrant brush and massage cycle in three minutes.  There aren&#x27;t many times I can&#x27;t spare my teeth that extra two minutes, and my dental health is important.  After running through the brush and massage cycle for each of the four quadrants (upper front, upper back, lower front, and lower back), the toothbrush automatically shuts off.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;EASE OF USE&lt;br /&gt;There are a number of buttons on both the base charger/sanitizer and the cordless toothbrush, but they are simple to learn and easy to use.  After checking the manual once on how to activate the cleaning routines, I&#x27;ve not needed to consult it again for this information.  The sanitizer activates with a simple push of the button on top of the unit and shuts off automatically when it completes the sanitizing cycle.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;QUALITY/DURABILITY&lt;br /&gt;Of course, I&#x27;ll be better able to report on this area in a year, but the product seems sturdy and built for long-term use, unlike some hardware which feels more like it is made for disposability.  The product inspires confidence in me that Philips truly means this unit to last the consumer for many years, only needed to replace consumable parts such as the toothbrush heads periodically.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;VALUE&lt;br /&gt;This area is the real kicker.  I love the toothbrush, and find myself extremely satisfied with all of its parts and features, as well as the results of brushing with it diligently for almost three weeks.  Is it worth the initial investment?  I think that is a question better answered by looking at your own budget and how important your dental health is to you.  The general person will not likely spend this much on a toothbrush, sonic or not.  In fact, it is the pricing on these units that made me waffle over the decision to invest in one for the last year.  Having used it, I am now confident that it is worth the price, and am looking forward to fewer dental visits, other than the general check-ups necessary.  Again, only time will tell here if that is wishful thinking on my part or a true benefit.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In the end, this is no doubt a luxury item for most, more likely to end up under the Christmas tree for those who are interested in a sonic toothbrush.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;QUICK RECAP - PROS &amp; CONS&lt;br /&gt;Easy to use - I adapted easily to the button functions on the unit.&lt;br /&gt;Durable - the parts feel sturdy and built to last.&lt;br /&gt;Pricing a little high for most - more likely a luxury expense or gift item.&lt;br /&gt;Replacement parts - Brush heads are easily ordered through [...], but I am uncertain if they can be purchased in local stores.
