    <li> I have to admit that I was quite a bit skeptical about the Philips Sonicare Toothbrush. I&#x27;ve used electronic toothbrushes (all battery operated) in the past, and never saw a compelling difference between using them versus the traditional &#x27;manual&#x27; toothbrush.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So, trepiditiously, I tried the Sonicare....&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The device itself was easy to install (you&#x27;ll have to wait two hours after initially charging the unit before you can use it). The toothbrush comes with a handy gauge that indicates its charge.  Using the Sonicare was extremely easy - there&#x27;s a button on the back of the toothbrush unit that you have to press in order to activate the brush. One thing I quickly learned is to not turn the toothbrush &#x27;on&#x27; with toothpaste before putting it in your mouth - doing so will result in your toothpaste lining the base of your sink instead of your mouth.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The unit isn&#x27;t overly noisy, at least to me. Brushing was easy, unobtrusive, and fairly comfortable overall. The smaller toothbrush head makes it easy to clean those hard-to-reach places - leaving my teeth and gums shiny and my breath fresh. One thing I like in particular with the Sonicare is that you do not have to apply any force while brushing. (The common cause for gums to recede is usually due to over-brushing). You simply move the toothbrush around, and the brush vibrations take care of the rest.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;There are 5 brushing modes you can choose from, including one for sensitive teeth. The package also includes a travel charger and a UV sanitizer, which kills any germs which may live on your toothbrush.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;For most people, this unit is overkill - but it is well thought out and works well for its intended function. I personally enjoy using mine and would recommend it without reservation.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Update: my Philips Sonicare died last week. I called Customer Service up. They sent a new one out in 3 days (with no cost to me) and provided return shipping to send the old unit back. Excellent customer service!ellent customer service!</li>
    <li> The Sonicare FlexCare has a mind / programing of it&#x27;s own which for me is a good thing.  Sometimes I&#x27;m in a rush to head out the door and don&#x27;t realize how little I did actually brush my teeth.  With this toothbrush not anymore!  It has timed programs and beeps to let you know to move onto the next section of teeth!  I started with the sensitive program which found out later by reading more of the manual it actually increases the level of sensitivity over the course of 14 brushings!  I love that it&#x27;s not harsh on my teeth which I consider to be sensitive (It wasn&#x27;t until the age of 31 that I had my first filling).  It says it leaves you with a Dentist office clean which I agree whole heartedly and in my case without any of the pain that I would typically be in from keeping my mouth open and having them clean my sensitive teeth!    I like how the toothbrush head and handle is small, actually smaller then the manual toothbrush I had been using! I have a small mouth so it&#x27;s great!  I feel better knowing it has the UV Sanitizing feature which kills 99% of germs on the brush head!      Overall I&#x27;m extremely surprised and happy with this product and believe I&#x27;ll be looking forward to a shorter cleaning time at the Dentist Office!</li>
    <li> UPDATE - Two Years Later&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It&#x27;s been more than two years with the Sonicare Flexcare for me and more than 10 years using Sonicare toothbrushes exclusively, save for trips where I took a non-electric standard toothbrush with me.  I can say that it&#x27;s time for me to move on and move back to the world of non-electric toothbrushes, and hence lower my original score of a 4 to a 3.  Let&#x27;s see why:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Durability: this is an issue that bothers me because the handle with the soft rubber began peeling/coming off after just a year of normal use.  When I received the Flexcare I wondered about durability of the soft handle since I knew from using previous Sonicare models that the hard plastic handles were very durable, and only yellowed over time.  A $150 toothbrush should not look like this with normal use.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Other issues: another issue I have is that the timer is only for two minutes, though this is the case with nearly every electric toothbrush, two minutes is just not enough time for me.  Another issue is cleaning the Flexcare which is as much a chore as it was with previous models.  Finally, the quality of the brusheads appear to have changed when they went to the brushead indicator rather than the sticker expiration date system.  Finally, the brushead is just too small for me, though it is nice that I get to feel when I brush each individual tooth.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;High points: Customer service is top notch.  I had two minor issues and they were ironed out very quickly.  Unlike many reviewers, aside from the cosmetic durability, I had no problem with the toothbrush.  I also had no problem with the battery life and I think this is key - I NEVER KEPT THE BASE PLUGGED IN.  No matter what others say, it seems that keeping the Flexcare on the stand will diminish battery life.  Finally, the toothbrush works and I believe that sanitation system also works.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Why I&#x27;m moving back to a regular toothbrush: that said, the cost of the brusheads is just too much, cosmetically the toothbrush is done, and I&#x27;ve come to the point where I feel that this toothbrush offers nothing over standard toothbrushes.  A few times over the years I used a Swissco brand toothbrush and recently began using a Radius Original toothbrush three times a day.  The size of the head is huge and the bristles much softer than the Sonicare.  After using it for a few months, my dentist noticed that my teeth were as good as when I was using the Sonicare - plus the Radius lasts me 9 months, 3 times longer than each Sonicare brushead.  I&#x27;m not sure what the verdict will be in the longrun, but I feel that if I continue to brush for at least two minutes, there won&#x27;t be a difference.  While I enjoyed my time using Sonicare, I feel at this point it is a luxury and doesn&#x27;t offer me anything more than a standard, albeit special kind, of toothbrush.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;ORIGINAL REVIEW&lt;br /&gt;I had two Sonicare Advances that lasted me eight or so years, then I took a three year break and used a manual toothbrush.  Last month I bought the Flexcare and the improvements over the Advance are drastic.  The brush is contoured, the unit is easy to grip and light, and there is no moldy gunk buildup anymore because the brush head snaps onto the brush.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;m taking a star off because the unit is a little loud when I&#x27;m brushing, but there is almost no vibration, so I guess that is the tradeoff.  Also, I could have done without the UV Sanitizer, but I do use it at least once a week, especially when I have a cold.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Also, customer service is really excellent.  The little Phillips logo on the travel case arrived broken, and when I contacted Sonicare, they said they would ship me a new one out for free without me having to send my broken one back.  The customer service representative even called me back when my phone lost reception.  Overall a great brush and company, Sonicare makes brushing fun!</li>

    <li> The number of options available with this toothbrush is wonderful.  Also the cleaning apparatus is a great addition.  I would have liked to receive a docking station that would hold 2 brush heads, as my husband and I both use one Sonicare and switch out the brush heads.</li>
    <li> First, let me preface this review by stating that since the early 2000&#x27;s I have been a user of the Sonicare line of toothbrushes.  Their cleaning capabilities is second to none and they are an excellent choice for teeth and gum health.  So then, why the 1 star review?  So that Phillips will pay attention to a glaring design quality issue in their FlexCare models.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Unfortunately, the reliability of the Sonicare toothbrushes has dramatically declined since the release of the FlexCare series.  I personally have gone through two toothbrushes in four years.  That is unacceptable when considering the cost of the units (~180 per unit), and when considering the lifespan of my previous and my wife&#x27;s current \\&quot;e-Series\\&quot; Sonicare toothbrushes (at 5+ and 6+ years respectively).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Sonicare FlexCare line of toothbrushes, out since 2008/2009, uses a significantly different design to attach the brush heads to the handle:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;*  In the older e-Series units, the connection was performed via a screw top connection to the handle.  The vibration was generated internally in the handle and transmitted to the brush head by means of metal feet in the brush head, resting on the top of the interior of the brush handle.  This made for a robust, and reliable connection.&lt;br /&gt;*  The newer FlexCare series has the vibration carried externally to a metal pole, which then slides inside of the brush head.  This new design has several internal attachment pieces that hold the metal rod in place.  This system of internally mounting the metal vibration pole is much more fragile than the previous system and is the weak link in terms of reliability.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Over time, each of my purchased FlexCare model Sonicare toothbrushes has had its internal mounts snap, causing a significant loss of vibration and cleaning power, with a simultaneous increase in noise.  It took 2 years in the previous unit, and 1 year in the most recently purchased unit.  This lack of reliability makes the value of the purchase decrease dramatically.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Given all of the above, if you can, please steer clear of the FlexCare units and purchase the older e Series units instead.  They provide the same level of cleaning power, but with the added benefit of much more reliability over multiple years of use.e value of the purchase decrease dramatically.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Given all of the above, if you can, please steer clear of the FlexCare units and purchase the older e Series units instead.  They provide the same level of cleaning power, but with the added benefit of much more reliability over multiple years of use.</li>
    <li> My toothbrush was great initially but then started turning itself on and off throughout the day without provocation. And believe me, when it&#x27;s 4am and your toothbrush starts buzzing like crazy from the other room, it is REALLY ANNOYING. Do yourself a favor and buy a different brand. Sonicare does NOT stand for quality.</li>
